Instead, <a href="/wiki/Diethyl_ether" title="Diethyl ether">diethyl ether</a>, being a stronger and more potent anaesthetic, was demonstrated and accepted for use in October 1846, along with <a href="/wiki/Chloroform" title="Chloroform">chloroform</a> in 1847.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug_discovery_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-Drug_discovery-13">[13]</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Thomas_Clover" title="Joseph Thomas Clover">Joseph Thomas Clover</a> invented the "gas-ether inhaler" in 1876, however, it became a common practice at hospitals to initiate all anaesthetic treatments with a mild flow of nitrous oxide, and then gradually increase the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anaesthesia" title="Anaesthesia">anaesthesia</a> with the stronger ether or chloroform. Clover's gas-ether inhaler was designed to supply the patient with nitrous oxide and ether at the same time, with the exact mixture being controlled by the operator of the device. It remained in use by many hospitals until the 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-use_in_dentistry_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-use_in_dentistry-14">[14]</a></sup> Although hospitals today are using a more advanced <a href="/wiki/Anaesthetic_machine" title="Anaesthetic machine">anaesthetic machine</a>, these machines still use the same principle launched with Clover's gas-ether inhaler, to initiate the anaesthesia with nitrous oxide, before the administration of a more powerful anaesthetic.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_patent_medicine">As a patent medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: As a patent medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Colton's popularization of nitrous oxide led to its adoption by a number of less than reputable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quacksalver" title="Quacksalver">quacksalvers</a>, who touted it as a cure for <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">consumption</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scrofula" title="Scrofula">scrofula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catarrh" title="Catarrh">catarrh</a>, and other diseases of the blood, throat, and lungs. Nitrous oxide treatment was administered and licensed as a <a href="/wiki/Patent_medicine" title="Patent medicine">patent medicine</a> by the likes of <a href="/wiki/C._L._Blood" title="C. L. Blood">C. L. Blood</a> and Jerome Harris in Boston and Charles E. Barney of Chicago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alleged_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-alleged-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-man_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-man-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Reviewing various methods of producing nitrous oxde is published.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatalysisToday2005_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-CatalysisToday2005-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_methods">Industrial methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Industrial methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nitrous_oxide_production.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Nitrous_oxide_production.png/220px-Nitrous_oxide_production.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Nitrous_oxide_production.png/330px-Nitrous_oxide_production.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Nitrous_oxide_production.png/440px-Nitrous_oxide_production.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nitrous_oxide_production.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nitrous oxide production</div></div></div>
<p>Nitrous oxide is prepared on an industrial scale by careful heating of <a href="/wiki/Ammonium_nitrate" title="Ammonium nitrate">ammonium nitrate</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatalysisToday2005_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-CatalysisToday2005-84">[84]</a></sup> at about 250 C, which decomposes into nitrous oxide and water vapour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span>NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>  → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span>  + <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span></dd></dl>
<p>The addition of various <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a> salts favours formation of a purer gas at slightly lower temperatures. This reaction may be difficult to control, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Detonation" title="Detonation">detonation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Laboratory_methods">Laboratory methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Laboratory methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The decomposition of ammonium nitrate is also a common laboratory method for preparing the gas. Equivalently, it can be obtained by heating a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Sodium_nitrate" title="Sodium nitrate">sodium nitrate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ammonium_sulfate" title="Ammonium sulfate">ammonium sulfate</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">NaNO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + (<span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>)<sub>2</sub><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">Na<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span>+ 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span>.</dd></dl>
<p>Another method involves the reaction of urea, nitric acid, and sulfuric acid:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>2  (NH<sub>2</sub>)<sub>2</sub>CO  + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">HNO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>+ <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> + (NH<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> + 2<span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span>.</dd></dl>
<p>Direct oxidation of ammonia with a <a href="/wiki/Manganese_dioxide" title="Manganese dioxide">manganese dioxide</a>-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bismuth_oxide" title="Bismuth oxide">bismuth oxide</a> catalyst has been reported:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> cf. <a href="/wiki/Ostwald_process" title="Ostwald process">Ostwald process</a>.
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> + 3 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span></dd></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hydroxylammonium_chloride" title="Hydroxylammonium chloride">Hydroxylammonium chloride</a> reacts with <a href="/wiki/Sodium_nitrite" title="Sodium nitrite">sodium nitrite</a> to give nitrous oxide. If the nitrite is added to the hydroxylamine solution, the only remaining by-product is salt water. If the hydroxylamine solution is added to the nitrite solution (nitrite is in excess), however, then toxic higher oxides of nitrogen also are formed:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>OH</span><span class="chemf nowrap">Cl</span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">NaNO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> + NaCl + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span></dd></dl>
<p>Treating <span class="chemf nowrap">HNO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> with <span class="chemf nowrap">SnCl<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> and HCl also has been demonstrated:
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">HNO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + 8 HCl + 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">SnCl<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → 5 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> + 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">SnCl<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span></dd></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hyponitrous_acid" title="Hyponitrous acid">Hyponitrous acid</a> decomposes to N<sub>2</sub>O and water with a <a href="/wiki/Half-life" title="Half-life">half-life</a> of 16 days at 25 °C at  pH 1–3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wiberg&amp;Holleman_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wiberg&amp;Holleman-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>H<sub>2</sub>N<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>→ H<sub>2</sub>O + N<sub>2</sub>O</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Atmospheric_occurrence">Atmospheric occurrence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Atmospheric occurrence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nitrous oxide is a minor component of Earth's atmosphere, currently with a <a href="/wiki/Concentration" title="Concentration">concentration</a> of about 0.330 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parts_per_million" title="Parts per million">ppm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clim_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-clim-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emissions_by_source">Emissions by source</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Emissions by source">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, it was estimated that about 29.5 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_ton" title="Metric ton">tonnes</a> of <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> (containing 18.8 million tonnes of nitrogen) were entering the atmosphere each year; of which 64% were natural, and 36% due to human activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inputs_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-inputs-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa.gov_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa.gov-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> emitted into the atmosphere, from natural and anthropogenic sources, is produced by <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> in soils and oceans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sloss1992_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sloss1992-94">[94]</a></sup> Soils under natural vegetation are an important source of nitrous oxide, accounting for 60% of all naturally produced emissions. Other natural sources include the oceans (35%) and atmospheric chemical reactions (5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inputs_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-inputs-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>The main components of anthropogenic emissions are fertilized agricultural soils and livestock manure (42%), runoff and leaching of fertilizers (25%), biomass burning (10%), fossil fuel combustion and industrial processes (10%), biological degradation of other nitrogen-containing atmospheric emissions (9%), and human <a href="/wiki/Sewage" title="Sewage">sewage</a> (5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denman_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-denman-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epaUpdated_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-epaUpdated-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Agriculture enhances nitrous oxide production through soil cultivation, the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fertiliser" title="Nitrogen fertiliser">nitrogen fertilisers</a>, and animal waste handling. These activities stimulate naturally-occurring bacteria to produce more nitrous oxide. Nitrous oxide emissions from soil can be challenging to measure as they vary markedly over time and space, and the majority of a year's emissions may occur when conditions are favorable during "hot moments"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and/or at favorable locations known as "hotspots".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among industrial emissions, the production of <a href="/wiki/Nitric_acid" title="Nitric acid">nitric acid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adipic_acid" title="Adipic acid">adipic acid</a> are the largest sources of nitrous oxide emissions. The adipic acid emissions specifically arise from the degradation of the <a href="/wiki/Nitrolic_acid" title="Nitrolic acid">nitrolic acid</a> intermediate derived from nitration of cyclohexanone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denman_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-denman-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biological_processes">Biological processes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Biological processes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Natural processes that generate nitrous oxide may be classified as <a href="/wiki/Nitrification" title="Nitrification">nitrification</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denitrification" title="Denitrification">denitrification</a>. Specifically, they include:
</p>
<ul><li>aerobic autotrophic nitrification, the stepwise oxidation of <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>) to <a href="/wiki/Nitrite" title="Nitrite">nitrite</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>) and to <a href="/wiki/Nitrate" title="Nitrate">nitrate</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>) (e.g., Kowalchuk and Stephen, 2001),</li>
<li>anaerobic heterotrophic denitrification, the stepwise reduction of <span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> to <span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>, <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">nitric oxide</a> (NO), <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> and ultimately <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>, where facultative anaerobe bacteria use <span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> as an electron acceptor in the respiration of organic material in the condition of insufficient oxygen (<span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>) (e.g. Knowles, 1982), and</li>
<li>nitrifier denitrification, which is carried out by autotrophic <span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>−oxidizing bacteria and the pathway whereby ammonia (<span class="chemf nowrap">NH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>) is oxidised to nitrite (<span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>), followed by the reduction of <span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> to nitric oxide (NO), <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> and molecular nitrogen (<span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>) (e.g., Webster and Hopkins, 1996; Wrage et al., 2001).</li>
<li>heterotrophic nitrification (Robertson and Kuenen, 1990)</li>
<li>aerobic denitrification by the same heterotrophic nitrifiers (Robertson and Kuenen, 1990)</li>
<li>fungal denitrification (Laughlin and Stevens, 2002)</li>
<li>non-biological chemodenitrification (e.g. Chalk and Smith, 1983; Van Cleemput and Baert, 1984; Martikainen and De Boer, 1993; Daum and Schenk, 1998; Mørkved et al., 2007)</li></ul>
<p>These processes are affected by soil chemical and physical properties such as the availability of mineral nitrogen and organic matter, acidity, and soil type; as well as climate-related factors such as soil temperature and water content (e.g., Mosier, 1994; Bouwman, 1996; Beauchamp, 1997; Yamulki et al. 1997; Dobbie and Smith, 2003; Smith et al. 2003; Dalal et al. 2003).
</p><p>The emission of the gas to the atmosphere is limited greatly by its consumption inside the cells, by a process catalyzed by the enzyme <a href="/wiki/Nitrous-oxide_reductase" title="Nitrous-oxide reductase">nitrous oxide reductase</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Environmental impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenhouse_effect">Greenhouse effect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Greenhouse effect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="676" data-file-width="1012" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png/220px-Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png/330px-Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png/440px-Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Major_greenhouse_gas_trends.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greenhouse gas trends</div></div></div>
<p>Nitrous oxide has a significant <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">global warming potential</a> as <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a>. On a per-molecule basis, considered over a 100-year-period, nitrous oxide has 298 times the atmospheric heat-trapping ability of carbon dioxide (<span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overview_of_greenhouse_gases_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overview_of_greenhouse_gases-106">[106]</a></sup> however, because of its low concentration (less than 1/1000 of that of <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clim_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-clim-91">[91]</a></sup> its contribution to the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">greenhouse effect</a> is less than one-third that of carbon dioxide, and also less than water vapour and methane. On the other hand, since 38% or more of the <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> entering the atmosphere is the result of human activity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-denman_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-denman-95">[95]</a></sup> and its concentration has increased 15% since 1750,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clim_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-clim-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> control of nitrous oxide is considered part of efforts to curb greenhouse gas emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2008 study by Nobel Laureate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Crutzen" title="Paul Crutzen">Paul Crutzen</a> suggests that the amount of nitrous oxide release attributable to agricultural nitrate fertilizers has been seriously underestimated, most of which presumably, would come under soil and oceanic release in the Environmental Protection Agency data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_layer_depletion">Ozone layer depletion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ozone layer depletion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nitrous oxide also has been implicated in <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">thinning of the ozone layer</a>. A new study suggests that <span class="chemf nowrap">N<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> emission currently is the single most important ozone-depleting substance (ODS) emission and is expected to remain the largest throughout the twenty-first century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sciozo_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-sciozo-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legality">Legality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nitrous_oxide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Legality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, possession of nitrous oxide is legal under federal law and is not subject to <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">DEA</a> purview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccle_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccle-111">[111]</a></sup> It is, however, regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> under the Food Drug and Cosmetics Act; prosecution is possible under its "misbranding" clauses, prohibiting the sale or distribution of nitrous oxide for the purpose of <a href="/wiki/Recreational_drug_use" title="Recreational drug use">human consumption</a>.
</p><p>Many states have laws regulating the possession, sale, and distribution of nitrous oxide. Such laws usually ban distribution to minors or limit the amount of nitrous oxide that may be sold without special license.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, in the state of California, possession for recreational use is prohibited and qualifies as a misdemeanour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_London_Borough_Council" title="Lambeth London Borough Council">Council</a> of the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Lambeth" title="London Borough of Lambeth">London Borough of Lambeth</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>) banned the use of the drug for recreational purposes, making offenders liable to an on-the-spot fine of up to £1,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Ministry_of_Health" title="New Zealand Ministry of Health">Ministry of Health</a> has warned that nitrous oxide is a prescription medicine, and its sale or possession without a prescription, is an offense under the Medicines Act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> This statement would seemingly prohibit all non-medicinal uses of nitrous oxide, although it is implied that only recreational use will be targeted legally.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, transfer of nitrous oxide from bulk cylinders to smaller, more transportable E-type, 1590 liter-capacity tanks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> is legal when the intended use of the gas is for medical anaesthesia.
</p>
